{
 "cells": [
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "# Influence of the filters\n",
    "\n",
    "Only wavelet filters were used in the previous notebooks, but some finite difference filters are also provided in SiegPy. The goal of this notebook is to compare the results obtained with these other filters to the default results."
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "## Initialization\n",
    "\n",
    "The initialization only consists in importing the relevant classes and modules and defining a potential and a particular coordinate mapping."
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "### Import some modules and classes"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "code",
   "execution_count": 1,
   "metadata": {},
   "outputs": [],
   "source": [
    "from siegpy import (Hamiltonian, SWPotential, ErfKGCoordMap, Gaussian,\n",
    "                    SWPBasisSet, FD2_filters, FD8_filters)\n",
    "import numpy as np"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "### Define a potential"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "code",
   "execution_count": 2,
   "metadata": {},
   "outputs": [],
   "source": [
    "# The potential is read from a file...\n",
    "siegerts = SWPBasisSet.from_file(\"siegerts.dat\")\n",
    "pot = siegerts.potential\n",
    "# ... and then discretized over a grid\n",
    "l = pot.width\n",
    "xmax = 7.5\n",
    "xgrid = np.linspace(-xmax, xmax, 501)\n",
    "pot.grid = xgrid"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "### Define a coordinate mapping"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "code",
   "execution_count": 3,
   "metadata": {},
   "outputs": [],
   "source": [
    "theta = 0.6\n",
    "x0 = 6.0\n",
    "lbda = 1.5\n",
    "cm = ErfKGCoordMap(theta, x0, lbda, grid=xgrid)"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "## Compare the filters\n",
    "\n",
    "Three family of filters are available within `Siegpy`, presented here by increasing length:\n",
    "\n",
    "- The finite difference filters of order 2 `FD2_filters`,\n",
    "\n",
    "- The finite difference filters of order 8 `FD8_filters`,\n",
    "\n",
    "- The wavelet filters `Sym8_filters` (used as default).\n",
    "\n",
    "The filter used is defined at the Hamiltonian initialization level:"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "code",
   "execution_count": 4,
   "metadata": {},
   "outputs": [],
   "source": [
    "ham_1 = Hamiltonian(pot, cm, filters=FD2_filters)\n",
    "ham_2 = Hamiltonian(pot, cm, filters=FD8_filters)\n",
    "ham_3 = Hamiltonian(pot, cm) # default Sym8_filters"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "The three hamiltonians are then solved as usual:"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "code",
   "execution_count": 5,
   "metadata": {},
   "outputs": [],
   "source": [
    "basis_1 = ham_1.solve()\n",
    "basis_2 = ham_2.solve()\n",
    "basis_3 = ham_3.solve()"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "The eigenstates can then be compared by plotting the spectrum and the virial expectation value for each state:"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "code",
   "execution_count": 6,
   "metadata": {},
   "outputs": [

    "It is worth noting that the same bound and resonant states are found using the three filters. The only (important) difference concerns the expectation values of the virial operators, that are not sufficiently low for the resonant states found using both finite difference filters. Still, using the basis set obtained with the finitie difference filters of order 8 allows to get the same results as the default wavelet filters when it comes to study the convergence of the completeness relation:"
